#### X Article

> What if I told you every single time you tried to make your AI agent system better, you're probably making it much worse. And you likely have no idea why either. I spent the last 3 weeks or so learning this the hard way. And the worst part about it is I did it to myself, over and over again. Now here's exactly how it happened.
>
> I'd see someone post a badass prompt, an article, or YouTube video about OpenClaw thinking "damn that's smart", and send it straight to my agent system thinking it would improve things. Another person's tips on their orchestration framework? Send it over. Someone's skill configuration? Import it in. A new memory system on the timeline? Dump it in.
> And every single time, instead of simply improving the system, it broke things that were already working multiple times over. The new config would conflict with existing rules. The imported skills would collide with skills I already had. The governance framework would rewrite assumptions my routing depended on. I was context poisoning my own system with good intentions. And there's way more people out there doing the exact same thing too. The more I tried to make my system better by importing in other people's approaches, the worse my system got.
> The turning point was when I stopped doing that and started asking different questions. Instead of "what can I find on my timeline to absorb today?", it became "what's actually wrong with this system right now or my own? What did this system help improve this week? What broke and why did it break when we implemented it? What should we intelligently improve? What gaps aren't covered?" Structured reflection instead of impulse importing things into my system. Auditing what exists before bolting on something new.
> That shift in logic is what took my own system score from a 4.2 out of 10 on reliability and trust to something that actually reliably works (most of the time).
> That 4.2/10 wasn't because my system was inherently bad. It was because everything within it was lying to me and it was driving me fucking crazy frankly. Stale docs that it told me were current. Agents saying "done" when nothing was actually done or it hallucinated new context in.
>
> Rules I wrote in 3 different files getting violated in the same session they were cited in. Even corrections I gave the agent that somehow magically vanished the next day. System health scores that said everything was fine while critical stuff was failing underneath and I had no idea. And half of those problems were caused by me dumping in outside configs that didn't fit my own setup.
> And yes, eventually I fixed all of it. Every single damn thing that broke my system (and me frankly) got documented and turned into something reinforced and mechanical so it couldn't happen again.
>
> What follows below is everything I learned, what those failures actually looked like, and what I built to make my own system stop gaslighting me.
> This isn't something you skim and forget. Bookmark it now. Save it. Come back to it every time your agents start doing things you didn't ask for, or worse, telling you they did things they didn't actually do. You'll need it.
> Let's get into it.
>
> 1. Your Words Trigger Wrong Actions
> When I first set up my OpenClaw, I used loose word matching for action commands. Things like "go" and "proceed" as trigger words. The problem with that is those words show up in normal conversation all the time, so those commands were firing when they shouldn't have been. The agent would do something completely insane and I'd spend an hour figuring out why.
> The fix was embarrassingly simple. Use exact whole word matching instead of fuzzy word matching. Essentially, stop trying to be super clever with your routing and just be explicit about what triggers what. The collision that actually broke my orchestration layer came from a phrase nobody would have thought to test for either. That's why it was such a painful process to debug.
> And that's the other lesson here: if you're only testin...

### @masondrxy 

- Author: Mason Daugherty [@masondrxy](https://x.com/masondrxy)
- Tweet URL: [https://x.com/masondrxy/status/2031798630177251514](https://x.com/masondrxy/status/2031798630177251514)
- X article: [Autonomous context compression](https://x.com/masondrxy/article/2031798630177251514)
- X article text: TL;DR: We’ve added a tool to the Deep Agents SDK (Python) and CLI that allows models to compress their own context windows at opportune times. Motivation Context compression is an action that reduces the information in an agent’s working memory. Older messages are replaced by a summary or...
- Sources: bookmark@CatHanami97880
- Saved by: CatHanami97880
- Tweet created: 2026-03-11T18:25:17.000Z
- First seen: 2026-05-13T14:38:53Z
- Primary URLs:
  - [x.com/i/article/2031793610581311488](https://x.com/i/article/2031793610581311488)
- Thread URLs: none captured
- Public metrics: bookmark_count=939, impression_count=160275, like_count=546, quote_count=10, reply_count=7, retweet_count=74

> https://x.com/i/article/2031793610581311488

#### X Article

> TL;DR: We’ve added a tool to the Deep Agents SDK (Python) and CLI that allows models to compress their own context windows at opportune times.
>
> Motivation
> Context compression is an action that reduces the information in an agent’s working memory. Older messages are replaced by a summary or condensed representation of an agent’s progress that preserves what’s relevant to a task. This action is often necessary to accommodate finite context windows and reduce context rot.
> Agent harnesses often control this by compacting at a fixed token threshold (`deepagents` uses model profiles to compact at 85% of any given model’s context limit). This design is suboptimal because there are good times and bad times to compact:
> It is not ideal to compact when you’re in the middle of a complex refactor;
> It is better to compact when you are starting a new task or otherwise believe that prior context will lose relevance.
> Many interactive coding tools feature a `/compact` command or similar, which allows users to manually trigger a context compression step at opportune times. We take this one step further in the latest release of `deepagents` and expose a tool to the agent that lets it trigger context compression itself. This enables more opportunistic compaction without requiring your application’s users to be aware of finite context windows or issue specific commands.
> This tool is currently enabled in Deep Agents CLI and opt-in in the `deepagents` SDK.
> We are generally bullish on the idea that harnesses should, where possible, “get out of the way” and take advantage of improvements in the underlying reasoning models. This is an instance of the bitter lesson: can we give agents more control over their own context to avoid tuning their harness by hand?
> When should we compact?
> There is a variety of situations that could warrant a context compression action.
> At clean task boundaries:
> A user signals that they are moving on to a new task for which earlier context is likely irrelevant
> The agent has finished a deliverable and the user acknowledges task completion
> After extracting a result from a large amount of context:
> The agent has obtained a fact, conclusion, summary, or other result by consuming a significant amount of context, as in a research task
> Before consuming a large amount of new context:
> The agent is about to generate a long draft
> The agent is about to read a large amount of new context
> Before entering a complex multi-step process:
> The agent is about to start a lengthy refactor, migration, multi-file edit, or incident response
> The agent has produced a plan and is about to begin executing the steps
> A decision has been made that supersedes prior context:
> New requirements have come to light that invalidate previous context
> There are many tangents or dead-ends that can be reduced to a summary
> Enumerating all possible scenarios is not practical, but our observation is that people and LLMs can identify these scenarios and compact at opportune times, saving the need for a compaction step later on when the context window is nearing its limit. You can read the guidance we provide the model around this tool in its system prompt.
> What happens when the tool is called?
> The tool is parametrized the same as the existing Deep Agents summarization middleware: we retain recent messages (10% of available context) and summarize what comes before. Recent messages, including the call to the compaction tool and associated response, are retained in the recent context.
>
> See example trace.
> How to use
> The tool is implemented as a separate middleware, so you can enable it by adding it to the middleware list in `create_deep_agent`:
>
> See the SDK docs for more details.
> In the CLI, simply call `/compact` when you’re ready to trim context or move onto a new task.
> Our experience with this feature
> We tuned this feature to be conservative. Deep Agents preserves all conversation history in its virtual filesystem, allowing for recovery of context post-summarization, but an erro...

### @Av1dlive 

- Author: Avid [@Av1dlive](https://x.com/Av1dlive)
- Tweet URL: [https://x.com/Av1dlive/status/2031784290183495766](https://x.com/Av1dlive/status/2031784290183495766)
- X article: [Harness Engineering: The Next $100B Layer in AI](https://x.com/Av1dlive/article/2031784290183495766)
- X article text: you probably think vibe-coding will make you a millionaire* but you are missing out on the $100B AI opportunity The Harness the execution layer that turns accessible frontier intelligence into work Welcome to the infrastructure market nobody's building for yet. p.s. I mean less people :) Where...
- Sources: bookmark@CatHanami97880
- Saved by: CatHanami97880
- Tweet created: 2026-03-11T17:28:18.000Z
- First seen: 2026-05-13T14:38:53Z
- Primary URLs:
  - [x.com/i/article/2031668106020659200](https://x.com/i/article/2031668106020659200)
  - [openai.com/index/harness-engineering](https://openai.com/index/harness-engineering/)
  - [x.com/Vtrivedy10/status/2031408954517971368?s=20](https://x.com/Vtrivedy10/status/2031408954517971368?s=20)
  - [www.ignorance.ai/p/the-emerging-harness-engineering](https://www.ignorance.ai/p/the-emerging-harness-engineering)
  - [arxiv.org/html/2603.05344v1](https://arxiv.org/html/2603.05344v1)
- Thread URLs: none captured
- Public metrics: bookmark_count=1214, impression_count=75763, like_count=574, quote_count=14, reply_count=24, retweet_count=64

> https://x.com/i/article/2031668106020659200

#### X Article

> you probably think vibe-coding will make you a millionaire*
>
> but you are missing out on the
>
> $100B AI opportunity
> The Harness
> the execution layer that turns accessible frontier intelligence into work
>
> Welcome to the infrastructure market nobody's building for yet.
>
> p.s. I mean less people :)
>
>
>
> Where did we go wrong ?
> Two years we have optimized for the wrong thing.
>
> The AI race was defined by model size, benchmarks, scores, and parameter counts.
>
> As agent systems moved from demos to actual deployments, something became painfully clear.
>
> For an useful agent, the model is no longer the moat . It's the Harness.
>
> A useful agent, as described by (@Vtrivedy10) latest article titled "The Anatomy of an Agent Harness" is simply the model + harness
>
>
> The New Abstraction: Agent = Model + Harness
> Modern agent  systems consist of three conceptual layers
> The model is the reasoning layer
> Harness is the execution system
> Agent app is the workflow built on top
> My fundamental thesis for this is that the next $100B AI infrastructure layer will not be another model lab/ thin agent application
>
> It will be the harness layer which includes
> The runtime
> The orchestration
> The tooling
> The memory
> The policy
> The sandboxing
> The verification
> The observability
> This is the stack that operationalizes modern intelligence
>
> 1. Why harnesses become control plane for ai systems
> The complexities of managing AI agents increase dramatically as it moves away from isolated prompts to long-running autonomous workflows
> Agents must now:
> Coordinate multiple tools
> Maintain state across tasks
> Operate within secure boundaries
> Manage execution environments
> Verify outcomes
>
> These requirements quickly transform agentic systems from simple model calls into distributed system problems.
> At that point, we see the architecture naturally separate into two layers, which mirrors the pattern seen in previous computing eras.
>  the model becomes the reasoning layer;
> the harness becomes the execution layer.
> This is similar to how operating systems separated application logic from hardware control.
> The agentic systems are converging towards the same structure as they scale in autonomy and complexity.
> This control layer becomes not just useful but necessary.
>
> 2. What a harness is (Technically)
> Harness is an execution system which is wrapped around a model.
>
> It provides the state, the environment, the control loops, and enforceable constraints
>
> Here are the key primitive and what they cater to:
> Prompt and policy layer - system prompts, behavioural constraints, safety policies & task instructions
> Durable state/file system - artefacts, logs, documentation & planning files
> Tool Registries/MCP layer- authentications, rate limits & permission boundaries
> Memory, context, and verification layer - retrieval , context compaction, verification loops and tracing/observability
>
> 3. Why raw models are insufficient
> More models can generate tokens but it cannot by itself
> Persist durable state
> Execute code safely
> Access internal and external systems
> Verify whether work succeeded
> Coordinate long horizon tasks
> All of these capabilities exist outside the model, which means that useful agent behavior is primarily a harness problem.
> The model provides the cognitive component, while the harness provides the execution infrastructure
>
> 4. How to build a Harness
> A typical harness architecture looks like this
>
> This architecture is a resemblance of a classic distributed systems design.
>
> The harness acts as the control plane, meanwhile the execution layer functions as the data plane.
>
> Core Harness Primitives in Practice
> In practice, most production Harnesses rely on a small set of foundational primitives which are :
> file system
> general-purpose runtimes
> sandboxing
> iterative verification mechanisms
> observability
>
> 5. Evidence that the harness  matters
> Harness engineering is not theoretical.
>
> Several experiments demonstrate that changing the Harness can dramatically improve agent performance.
>
> For example:
> LangChain improved a...

#### X Article

> You're paying for data that's already open. Someone just collected it in one place.
> What Is This?
> public-apispublic-apis is a GitHub repository. Inside - 1000+ public APIs on any topic. Free. Legal. Many require no keys at all.
> Most developers know about it.
> If you trade on Polymarket - this is your list of tools for a real information edge. Build tools, automate the routine, level up. No Bloomberg terminal needed.
> Categories:
>
> Finance & Crypto
>
> Quotes, charts, macro data, Fed rates, fear indexes.
> Examples: CoinGecko, CoinCap, Alpha Vantage, Open Exchange Rates, FRED.
>
> News & Media
>
> Headline parsing, RSS, aggregators, sentiment - in real time.
> Examples: NewsAPI, GNews, TheNewsAPI, MediaStack, New York Times API.
> Weather & Geolocation
>
> Temperature, precipitation, forecasts, historical data for any point on the planet.
> Examples: Open-Meteo (completely free), OpenWeatherMap, WeatherAPI, Visual Crossing.
> Sports & Statistics
>
> Results, team form, player stats, historical league data.
> Examples: API-Football, TheSportsDB, PandaScore, ESPN API.
> Machine Learning & Text Analysis
>
> Ready-made models for text classification, sentiment analysis, summarization, embeddings.
> Examples: Hugging Face Inference API, Cohere.
> Entertainment
>
> Streaming platform charts, movie ratings, music charts, gaming data.
> Examples: TMDB, RAWG, MusicBrainz.
> What You Can Build in a Weekend?
> News aggregator - NewsAPI + keyword filter + Telegram alerts. 2-3 hours.
> Sentiment scorer - news > Hugging Face model > score from -1 to +1 > signal.
> Weather dashboard - Open-Meteo + historical data + forecast for your target city.
> Sports tracker - team form, injuries, home advantage all in one place.
> How to Use the Repository?
> What to look at in the table:
> Auth - No means no registration required
> HTTPS - always Yes
> CORS - matters for frontend, not critical for scripts
> Limits - most free APIs have a daily limit, enough for personal tools
> The Scale We Didn't Cover
> We covered a small part. There's also politics, law, health, science, transport, government data.
> The best thing you can do feed the entire list to an AI agent and ask what's useful for your specific tasks. The agent will have something to work with. It will find connections you wouldn't notice yourself.

### @odysseus0z 

- Author: George [@odysseus0z](https://x.com/odysseus0z)
- Tweet URL: [https://x.com/odysseus0z/status/2031850264240800131](https://x.com/odysseus0z/status/2031850264240800131)
- X article: [Getting Started with OpenAI Symphony](https://x.com/odysseus0z/article/2031850264240800131)
- X article text: I pushed 50 tickets to Linear before bed — a tech debt rewrite of an Electron app. Woke up to 30 merged PRs. 7,000 net lines deleted. Two days later, nothing has broken. This is Symphony — OpenAI's open-source orchestrator for Codex agents. Point it at a Linear board and it turns tickets into...
- Sources: bookmark@CatHanami97880
- Saved by: CatHanami97880
- Tweet created: 2026-03-11T21:50:27.000Z
- First seen: 2026-05-13T14:38:53Z
- Primary URLs:
  - [x.com/i/article/2031521021342388224](https://x.com/i/article/2031521021342388224)
- Thread URLs: none captured
- Public metrics: bookmark_count=2090, impression_count=251209, like_count=874, quote_count=12, reply_count=22, retweet_count=54

> https://x.com/i/article/2031521021342388224

#### X Article

> I pushed 50 tickets to Linear before bed — a tech debt rewrite of an Electron app. Woke up to 30 merged PRs. 7,000 net lines deleted. Two days later, nothing has broken.
> This is Symphony — OpenAI's open-source orchestrator for Codex agents. Point it at a Linear board and it turns tickets into pull requests.
> I didn't even know how to properly test an Electron app. The agents figured it out — attaching to the running app over CDP via agent-browser, validating changes end-to-end, entirely self-directed. I'm learning how to test my own app by reading their logs.
> Set it up
> I maintain a fork that's easier to get started with (changes I made listed in README). From your project repo, run:
>
> Then tell your agent: "set up Symphony for my repo."
> For manual setup, follow the skill instruction manually.
> The Linear board is your control surface
> Everything happens through Linear. The board is the interface.
>
> Push a ticket to Todo — an idle agent claims it within seconds. Move a ticket to Rework with review comments — the agent picks it back up and addresses feedback.
> Start with a big idea, not individual tickets
> If you already have a well-organized Linear board, point Symphony at it and go. If you don't, have your agent play tech lead — describe the feature and let it decompose the work into tickets with dependencies mapped out.
> Give your agent access to Linear (official MCP setup) and hand it the big picture:
> Break this into tickets in project [slug]. Scope each ticket to one reviewable PR. Include acceptance criteria. Set blocking relationships where order matters.
> Push the batch to Todo and let Symphony parallelize across everything that isn't blocked.
> My 50-ticket Electron rewrite started as one conversation: "here's the tech debt, here's what I want the codebase to look like after." The agent decomposed it, I reviewed the tickets, adjusted a few, and pushed them to Todo.
> What to expect
> Each worker gets its own workspace clone, reads the ticket, writes a plan as a Linear comment, implements, validates, and opens a PR.
>
> The planning step is worth watching. Before writing code, the agent posts its plan as a Linear comment. Catch bad plans before they become bad PRs. It will check off todos it is done during the run, and give you a demo video at the end!
>
> One of my tickets asked for a ChatDisplay refactor — no mention of testing. The agent attached to the running Electron app over CDP via agent-browser, injected a temporary probe to force a render error, verified the failure was contained, clicked through recovery, screenshotted both states, and removed the probe. End-to-end validation of a UI change, entirely self-directed.
>
> Tune on the fly
> Cancel a ticket — the agent stops on the next poll. Move something back to Backlog to hold it. Push a batch to Todo to dispatch.
> WORKFLOW.md hot-reloads within a second — no restart needed. Common adjustments:
> agent.max_concurrent_agents — start at 2-3, scale up as you trust it
> agent.max_turns — turn limit per ticket. Higher for complex work, lower to cap token spend.
> What's actually doing the work
> Most of what makes this effective isn't the orchestrator — it's the prompt in WORKFLOW.md. Symphony is plumbing: poll Linear, dispatch workers, manage slots. The prompt teaches the agent how to plan, test, handle review feedback, and constrain scope.
> I'll dig into that prompt in a follow-up.

### @blackanger 这个 agent-spec 大家用了没？ 推荐大家使用，可以直接解锁 claude code 自主长时执行直到目标意图达到验收标准（ spec 中定义的）。

### @vikingmute 假如你使用Claude Code 配合本地模型，你会发现本地模型的推理速度下降大约90%，是因为 CC 自动在请求中添加了一个 Attribution Header，这个...

- Author: Viking [@vikingmute](https://x.com/vikingmute)
- Tweet URL: [https://x.com/vikingmute/status/2031356054865666054](https://x.com/vikingmute/status/2031356054865666054)
- Sources: bookmark@CatHanami97880
- Saved by: CatHanami97880
- Tweet created: 2026-03-10T13:06:38.000Z
- First seen: 2026-05-13T14:38:53Z
- Primary URLs:
  - [twitter.com/UnslothAI/status/2031123848729600371](https://twitter.com/UnslothAI/status/2031123848729600371)
- Thread URLs: none captured
- Public metrics: bookmark_count=1173, impression_count=122240, like_count=839, quote_count=5, reply_count=18, retweet_count=154

> 假如你使用Claude Code 配合本地模型，你会发现本地模型的推理速度下降大约90%，是因为 CC 自动在请求中添加了一个 Attribution Header，这个 header 会导致本地推理服务的 KV Cache 完全失效，从而使本地模型的推理速度下降 约 90%，一旦失效，相当于退化到几乎不使用缓存的状态，速度变得非常慢。 https://twitter.com/UnslothAI/status/2031123848729600371

### @haruruuun0405 

- Author: 清水はるか｜Lead Designer [@haruruuun0405](https://x.com/haruruuun0405)
- Tweet URL: [https://x.com/haruruuun0405/status/2054025973830684775](https://x.com/haruruuun0405/status/2054025973830684775)
- X article: [Design SystemのSkillの精度が上がった8つの方法](https://x.com/haruruuun0405/article/2054025973830684775)
- X article text: デザインシステムをSkill化しても、AIが中々言うことを聞いてくれなくて困っている人もいるかと思います。今日はそんな方向けに、同じファイルを色んなSkillを使ってひたすら改善し、その中で良かった方法を8つご紹介できればと思います。（※今回はデザインシステムの中でも、Design Tokenの話をさせていただきます。）サンプル数はまだ少なく精緻な情報ではないので、そこだけご容赦ください。 0. なぜSkill化すると良いのか...
- Sources: bookmark@chumsdock
- Saved by: chumsdock
- Tweet created: 2026-05-12T02:28:48.000Z
- First seen: 2026-05-13T09:17:40Z
- Primary URLs:
  - [x.com/i/article/2053872767976837120](https://x.com/i/article/2053872767976837120)
  - [www.tsuntech.jp](https://www.tsuntech.jp/)
  - [apps.apple.com/jp/app/onetomo/id6760103954](https://apps.apple.com/jp/app/onetomo/id6760103954)
- Thread URLs: none captured
- Public metrics: bookmark_count=335, impression_count=16699, like_count=218, quote_count=1, reply_count=1, retweet_count=19

> https://x.com/i/article/2053872767976837120

#### X Article

> デザインシステムをSkill化しても、AIが中々言うことを聞いてくれなくて困っている人もいるかと思います。今日はそんな方向けに、同じファイルを色んなSkillを使ってひたすら改善し、その中で良かった方法を8つご紹介できればと思います。（※今回はデザインシステムの中でも、Design Tokenの話をさせていただきます。）サンプル数はまだ少なく精緻な情報ではないので、そこだけご容赦ください。
> 0. なぜSkill化すると良いのか
> そもそもなぜSkill化すると良いのかについてですが、その中の一つに技術スタックが違ってもある程度共通のデザインを色んなプロダクトで取り入れられることにあると思っています。デザインシステムを色んなプロダクトに導入したいけど技術の制約があって中々難しい場合に、まず導入する入り口として非常に良いのではないかと個人的に感じています。
> 1. Design TokenをCSSにした
>
> それでは、まず1つ目のDesign TokenをCSSにしたことからご紹介します。AIにSkillを作ってと丸投げすると、まず最初はMarkdownでの記述がされていました。そこで、これってMarkdownが適切なのかね？と聞いてみたところ、CSSがいいんじゃないと言われたので、CSSに変えてみました。そして、Markdownとどっちのアウトプットの精度が上がったのか検証してみたのですが、「AIがまずチェックする項目がCSSの変数、その後に読み込むのがコメント」という情報の棲み分けがより簡単にでき、検証結果としてはCSSの方が高い精度を保つことができました。
> 2. Cursorのruleでダブルチェック
> 続いて、Cursorのrule機能でダブルチェックをすることによって、さらに検証の結果が良くなりました。これは、ruleじゃなくてもhook機能でダブルチェックをしても良いかもしれないのですが、個人的にはruleの軽さが好きなので、rule機能を使っています。
> Cursorのruleとは、AIへいつも従ってほしい方針を書いておく仕組みです。会話ごとに同じことを説明し直さなくても、コード規約やアーキテクチャ・命名・禁止事項などを常に読み込ませられます。
> そして、重要なのがruleのチェック項目かと思うのですが、以下のような形で、Step by Stepで実施をしています。
>
> 非常に良かったなと思う点として、AIがCSSの変数、その横のコメントを拾うようにしたことです。
> チェック項目1でまずハードコードがないかを洗い出し、2でCSS内の変数を使っているかを洗い出し、3でその横の変数と意味をすり合わせるという、AIにとって気持ちのいいワークフローを作れたんじゃないかなと思います。
> 3. CSSファイルを分割
> 次に、CSSファイルを分割してみることにしたら、さらに検証の結果が良くなりました。行数がめちゃくちゃ長いわけではないので一つのファイルにしていたのですが、ちょっとでもAIが読む行数が短い方がやっぱり良いみたいで、Color・TypographyなどtokenごとでCSSファイルを分割して、必要に応じて読ませることで、さらに精度が上がりました。
> 4. Primitivesを全面禁止
> 困ったこととして、「Semanticを優先する」みたいな書き方をしていた際に、Primitivesで良いものもめちゃくちゃSemanticを使ってくることが多く、一度Primitivesを全面禁止にしてみました。そうすると、全面禁止にしたとて、どのみちAIは勝手に判断してPrimitivesを提案したがるので結果的にいい具合の塩梅になりました。
> 5. 「等」に使用を「のみ」に使用に
> もう一つ困ったこととして、例外的に使って欲しいtokenをばりばりにAIが使ってくるという事例がありました。そこで、どんなコメントをつけていたかを見直してみると、
> 〇〇など特殊なタイミングに使用
> という非常に曖昧な書き方をしてしまっていました。そこで、
> 使用可: 〇〇のみ。通常は〇〇を使うこと。
> という限定的な書き方をしました。これも、Primitivesと同様に全面禁止にしたい訳ではなく場合によって使用してもいいタイミングもあるのですが、どのみちAIは勝手に判断して例外対応を使いたがるので結果的にいい具合の塩梅になりました。
> 6. 複数CSSをまたぐルールは別mdに
> 上記を全て試してもうまくいかない箇所がいくつかありました。それらをじっくり見てみると、複数CSSを跨いで判断しないといけない事例であることがわかりました。片方のCSSだけ読んでいるAIだと判別できなくなってしまうので、別のprohibitions.mdという横断ファイルを作成しました。
>
> これを設けてCSS横断のルールを記載することによって、複数CSSを跨いで判断するルールに関しても、AIが情報を読み取って、判断してくれるようになりました。
> 7. 人と同様のチェック手順を設ける
> 最後まで中々解決しなかったことが、入れ子の構造に応じたmarginルールを理解してもらうことです。どれだけ説明してもあまり守られなかったのですが、人と同じような気持ちになって「何をまずはチェックしたらいいか」、「その次に先ほどのチェックした要素と何を比べればいいか」といったチェック手順を設けてあげることで、一気にAIがルールを理解してくれるようになりました。
>
> 8. 粒度を合わせてダブりなく
> 行数が増えるごとに、だんだんファイルがぐちゃぐちゃになってしまうこともあるかと思います。しかし、そうすると段々AIが思ったところをうまく読んでくれないという沼にハマってしまいます。そこで私が実施したこととしては、当たり前かもしれませんが、1.1つのファイルの中身の情報の粒度を合わせること、2.似たような内容は一回しか書かないことです。
> AIはすぐ余計な文章を追加してくるので、「他にこれって書いてるところってなかったっけ？」「これってこのファイルに追加する情報で適切なんだっけ？」という視点を持つことが重要だと思います。
>
> 最後に
> いかがでしたでしょうか？もし気になる方法が見つかった方がいればぜひ試してみてください。
> ▼ちなみに色々アプリも出してるので、ぜひ覗いっていってください▼
> 本のおすすめSNS📕
> https://www.tsuntech.jp/
> 個人開発アプリの投票サイト🗳️
> https://apps.apple.com/jp/app/onetomo/id6760103954
> お散歩中わんちゃんの可視化アプリ🐶
> https://apps.apple.com/jp/app/onetomo/id6760103954
